"NEWBIE BARBARIAN"

    For a quick overview of who the barbarian is, type "help class
    barbarian".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this brutal class.

    'Practice' and get good at the skill 'bash'.

    The barbarian's gear is very difficult to come by, don't be
    discouraged if it feels like you can not pick up a lot of
    good looking items.

    You have a lot of 'hitpoints', don't be afraid to spend them
    during a fight, you will outlast opponents.

    Be careful using the skill 'berserk', you can not flee from
    a battle after berserking, don't bite off more than you can
    chew.

    The barbarian guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is
    in the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the barbarian guildmaster is
    s2e4n3wnen

#
"NEWBIE CLERIC"

    For a quick overview of who the cleric is, type "help class
    cleric".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this healing class.

    Do research on your spells before you 'practice' them, you
    might not want to 'practice' a weaker version of a spell if
    you can learn a more powerful version later, like the 'cure
    light' and 'cure serious' spells.

    When you learn a brand new spell, it is very expensive to
    'cast'.  As you gain levels, it will drop in cost, so the
    thing to do is to pretend you don't have that spell
    for a while.

    Try not to 'cast' healing spells during combat, it is very
    difficult to do so, and it is more likely to waste your
    'mana' than heal yourself or your target.

    When you can learn the spell 'animate dead' it might be
    worth it, you can use the zombie as a buffer between you
    and your opponents.

    Clerics really take off after level 26, so don't be
    discouraged if you struggle early on.

    The cleric guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the cleric guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w2swnw

#
"NEWBIE DRUID"

    For a quick overview of who the druid is, type "help class
    druid".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this nature guardian.

    Do research on your spells before you 'practice' them, you
    might not find every spell to be equally as useful, especially
    if you don't need a weaker version of a spell and can wait
    for the more powerful version, like the 'cure light' and
    'cure serious' spells.

    When you learn a brand new spell, it is very expensive to
    'cast'.  As you gain levels, it will drop in cost, so the
    thing to do is to pretend you don't have that spell
    for a while.

    Learn 'flame blade' when you get the opportunity.

    Be careful of your alignment, if you become too good or
    too evil, you lose your druidic powers, permanently.

    When you start being able to summon creatures to serve you,
    use them as buffers between yourself and your opponents.

    The druid guildmaster is inside the King's Grove in the northeast
    corner of town.  Go east from Market Square to inside the
    Eastern Gate, then head north into the King's Grove and she
    is in the eastern part.  From the Temple of Karsinya
    the druid guildmaster is s2e3n3e5nen

    When you reach level 10, you must start to duel with another
    druid to gain your next level.  You can find that challenge
    area in the large tree, all the way west of town.

#
"NEWBIE GENERAL"

    Welcome to mudding.  Derived from the pencil and paper
    versions of popular role playing games, this is a place
    where you can interact in real time with people from
    all over the globe in a fantasy setting.  The rules
    of how to play are governed by a program run on a
    computer rather than by a game master, or dungeon
    master.  You type commands, the program (usually
    referred to in general as the "mud") interprets what
    you typed, and it processes the information, inserting
    your action into the world.  Most of the commands
    are very intuitive, here are some basics to get you
    started (type the words in the double quotes and hit enter).

    To look around the room you are in type "look"
    To pick up a dagger that is lying in the room with you type "get dagger"
    To see your personal information type "score"
    To move about, type the first letter from a cardinal direction, such
        as: "n" for north, or "e" for east, or "u" for up.
    To see who is on the mud with you, type "who"

    Anytime you feel confused, feel free to "yell help me! I'm new!"
    The help is fairly extensive, type "help help help" to get
    information on how to best use it.
    There are help topics written for each character class for new
    players, try "help newbie " then your character class.  If you
    are a warrior, you would type "help newbie warrior".

    A full listing of the help topics available for new players can
    be found at "help newbie list", and a small map of the main
    town can be found at "help newbie map".  Directions to places
    is listed in speedwalk terminology, which looks like this:
    s2e4neu
    That translates to take go "south" once, go "east" twice, go
    "north" 4 times, go "east" once, and "up" once.  This is a
    very convenient way of expressing directions to other people.

    If you ever get very lost and confused try using the
    "recallhome" command to bring you back safely to town.

    When you are ready to end your visit, you should find an Inn
    to stay at while you are gone.  The Inn in Karsinya is just
    east and up from the Meeting Square.

    Have fun, enjoy yourself.

#
"NEWBIE MAGE"

    For a quick overview of who the mage is, type "help class
    mage".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this magic casting class.

    Do research on your spells before you 'practice' them, if
    a spell doesn't seem immediately useful, think about whether
    you want to learn it right now.  There is always time to learn
    it later if you change your mind.

    When you learn a brand new spell, it is very expensive to
    'cast'.  As you gain levels, it will drop in cost, so the
    thing to do is to pretend you don't have that spell
    for a while.

    'Magic missile' is the workhorse of the mage.  It has
    excellent damage potential, is fast to 'cast', and doesn't
    cost much 'mana'.  Get good at this spell and use it
    often.

    Try to find someone who will stand and get hit by your
    opponents, while you 'cast' spells safely from behind them.

    The early levels are difficult, but mages become extremely
    powerful in the later levels, so be patient and careful.

    The mage guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the mage guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w2nwsw

#
"NEWBIE MONK"

    For a quick overview of who the monk is, see "help class
    monk".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this martial arts master.

    While you can wield weapons as a monk, you are almost
    certainly better off using your fists.  Maybe for the
    first few levels you could use a weapon.

    'Legsweep' is a very useful skill, learn it well.

    Be careful of the fights you get into, if an opponent
    requires a magic weapon to hit them and you are not
    experienced enough, you will not be able to hit them
    with your fists.  Eventually, you can hit anything,
    but if you find yourself missing all the time in a
    fight, you might be experiencing this difficulty.

    Learn 'dodge', it's effects aren't very noticeable, but
    they add up over time.

    When you reach 10th level you must win a duel with another
    monk to advance in level.

    The monk guildmaster is outside the town of Karsinya in
    the Monk Monastery to the northwest of the town.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the monk guildmaster is
    s2e3n5w4n5w5n5e

#
"NEWBIE NECROMANCER"

    For a quick overview of who the necromancer is, see "help class
    necromancer".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this death mage.

    'Life tap' is a fantastic spell, which you should master as soon
    as you are able.

    As soon as you can start creating the undead, you should use them
    as fodder for your battles.

    Fight good aligned opponents, you receive significant damage
    bonuses against them, and significant penalties for fighting
    evil opponents.

    If you end up with over 100% of your hitpoints from 'life tap'
    and similar spells, use those hitpoints wisely, when the next
    'tick' occurs, you lose those excess hitpoints.

    The necromancer guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the necromancer guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w2n

#
"NEWBIE PALADIN"

    For a quick overview of who the paladin is, see "help class
    paladin".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this righteous warrior.

    Learn and master the spell 'cure light' because you don't
    receive another healing spell for a long time.

    'Holy strength', 'holy armor', and 'aura of power' are
    truly incredible abilities for the paladin, learn and use
    them as soon as you can.

    Fight evil aligned opponents, you receive significant damage
    bonuses against them, and significant penalties for fighting
    good opponents.

    Use 'call steed' when you are travelling from one place to
    another, it will save you 'move', and when needed, the
    mighty steed will fight for you.

    Learn and use 'spot', it makes adventuring much easier.

    The paladin guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the paladin guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w2sws

#
"NEWBIE PSIONIST"

    For a quick overview of who the psionist is, see "help class
    psionist".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this mental master.

    Learn and master the skill 'psionic blast', it is the most
    effective battle skill you will ever learn.

    Keep 'psi shield' up all the time, it provides good protection
    and improves as you gain levels.

    You learn 'doorway' early, use it when you know where you are
    going to save 'move'.  If you want to return to town, "doorway
    Zifnab" is a popular target.

    By the time you reach 15th level and learn 'flame shroud' you
    will probably be strong enough to start adventuring in Oblivion,
    a zone that is to the north of Karsinya.  Find the Shatterwood
    Forest and head north from there.  Oblivion has some very
    interesting equipment that only psionists can use.

    The psionist guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the psionist guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w3nw

#
"NEWBIE RANGER"

    For a quick overview of who the ranger is, see "help class
    ranger".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this nature warrior.

    Start to 'practice' 'dual wield' as soon as you can, so that you
    get your learning done early.

    'Bash' is your standard combat skill, so use it often.

    Fight evil aligned opponents, you receive significant damage
    bonuses against them.

    Practice and use 'spot', it makes adventuring much easier.

    The ranger guildmaster is in the Guild Hall to the west of the 
    Meeting Square.  From the Temple of Karsinya, the ranger guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w3sw

#
"NEWBIE RULES"

    The highest rule of the mud is the golden rule.  If you obey that,
    you will likely never be in violation of any of the other rules of
    the mud.  Punishments for failing to follow these rules vary, and
    is at the discretion of the adjucating immortal.
    
    1.  'Player Killing' outside of the 'Arena' is forbidden.  Even
        indirectly harming another player is illegal, such as summoning
        an unwilling player to a dangerous area.  Casting non-beneficial
        spells on another character is illegal as well.
        
    2.  Stealing from another character is illegal, even if you know them.
    
    3.  Kill stealing is illegal, which is when somebody has already
        started fighting a mob and you deal the final blow, robbing
        the original player of the experience.  When in doubt, ask.

    4.  Taking items off of the corpse of a recently deceased player
        is illegal.  Only if the player has given you permission should
        you get the items from a player's corpse.
        
    5.  Foul language will not be tolerated in any form, including
        replacing letters with symbols.  If you want to make your
        feelings known, get creative, cursing will be punished.
        
    6.  Whining, while not illegal, will certainly not win you any
        friends.
        
    7.  'Multi-playing' is illegal, if you are caught 'multi-playing'
        you will be punished.
        
    8.  Sharing characters is illegal, your password is sacred.  Do
        not share your character with friends, relatives, wives, 
        sons, etc.  And if your character gets hijacked by another
        person, the mud is not responsible for any damages that
        result from it.

    9.  "Bots" are illegal.  A bot is a set of scripts that automate
        your character to a greater extent than is acceptable by
        the mud.  It is a judgement call by the immortals on what
        constitutes a bot versus a set of triggers and scripts that
        aid a mudder.  Basically, if you don't have to be at your
        keyboard and your character is engaged in actions more
        complex than standing in one spot and keeping yourself from
        starving, you are probably close to bot-like activity.

#
"NEWBIE SORCERER"

    For a quick overview of who the sorcerer is, see "help class
    sorcerer".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this spell hurler.

    Do research on your spells before you 'practice' them, if
    a spell doesn't seem immediately useful, think about whether
    you want to learn it right now.  There is always time to learn
    it later if you change your mind.

    When you learn a brand new spell, it takes a very long time to
    'memorize'.  As you gain levels, it will get faster, so the
    thing to do is to pretend you don't have that spell
    for a while, or be willing to sit a long time.

    'Magic missile' is the workhorse of the mage.  It has
    excellent damage potential, is fast to 'recall', and doesn't
    take long to 'memorize'.  Get good at this spell and use it
    often.

    Try to find someone who will stand and get hit by your
    opponents, while you 'recall' spells safely from behind them.

    The early levels are difficult, but sorcerers become extremely
    powerful in the later levels, so be patient and careful.

    The sorcerer guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the sorcerer guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w2nese

#
"NEWBIE THIEF"

    For a quick overview of who the thief is, see "help class
    thief".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this backstabbing lowlife.

    'Backstab' is your friend, 'backstab' is your only friend.
    Learn it, get great at it.

    Use 'spy' often, it is difficult to get better at it, so
    the more often you try it, the faster you can learn it.

    Get used to having to 'flee', especially if you miss a
    'backstab'.  After you flee you will attempt to 'hide'
    automatically, so that if the opponent comes looking
    for you, you are ready to  'backstab' again.

    Do not be disappointed if you die, thieves tend to have
    low experience point requirements for levels, and can
    regain lost experience quickly.

    The thief guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the thief guildmaster is
    s2e4n4w2s2es

#
"NEWBIE WARRIOR"

    For a quick overview of who the warrior is, see "help class
    warrior".  Below are some strategies and tips for playing
    this sword swinger.

    'Bash' your way to victory, it is your primary combat skill,
    learn it and get good at it, it is valuable.

    Keep several weapons on hand, that way you can quickly 'draw'
    a new weapon if you are not having success with your current
    one and if you get 'disarm'ed, you don't have to waste time
    picking up the disarmed weapon.

    Early on, focus on finding items that have bonuses to 'hitroll'
    and armor.  Later in your career you can focus more on 'damroll'.

    When possible, practice 'rescue', because eventually you are
    going to save some poor magic user's life with that skill.

    The warrior guildmaster in the town of Karsinya is in
    the Guild Halls to the west of the Meeting Square.
    From the Temple of Karsinya, the warrior guildmaster is
    s2e4n3wses

#

"OBJ CLOSE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  close <container obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command is used in this context to close container objects
    that are open.  The 'close' command can also close doors, see
    'help move close'.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You wish to close the treasure chest after ransacking it.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> close chest
    Havok>  Ok.

#
"OBJ CORPSE"

    When mobs die, their bodies turn into corpses, which act as container
    objects.  Which means that they can be picked up and items taken from
    the corpse.  When you see a corpse and you wish to get the items that
    are "inside" that corpse, you use the 'get' command in the format of
    "get all corpse" or "get ring corpse".

#
"OBJ DONATE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  donate <obj | all | all.obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used when you have an extra piece of equipment
    that you don't need, but could be useful to others.  Using this
    command will cause the target object to disappear from your
    inventory and appear randomly in either the donation room in
    Karsinya or the one in New Thalos.  Using this command with
    the argument "all" will result in your entire inventory appearing
    in the donation rooms.  Or you can selectively donate all of one
    particular type of item by using the "all." argument, such as
    "all.dagger".

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: Your inventory has a spare dagger.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> donate dagger
    Havok>  a dagger disappears from your hands! A small voice says:
            'Thank you'.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: Your inventory has a bunch of useful gear in it, maybe
    some new player can use it.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> donate all
    Havok>  You donate everything you have! How generous!

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: Your inventory has four spare daggers.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> donate all.dagger
    Havok>  a dagger disappears from your hands! A small voice says:
            'Thank you'.
            a dagger disappears from your hands! A small voice says:
            'Thank you'.
            a dagger disappears from your hands! A small voice says:
            'Thank you'.
            a dagger disappears from your hands! A small voice says:
            'Thank you'.

#
"OBJ DRAW"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  draw <weapon obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting

    This command is used to instantly swap a wielded weapon with one
    in your inventory.  Be aware that if you can not wield the target
    weapon object, you might be left without any weapon wielded at
    all.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You are wielding a mace, but now wish to wield a dagger in
    your inventory.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> draw dagger
    Havok>  You stop using a mace and attempt to draw another weapon.

#
"OBJ DRINK"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  drink <liquid container obj | liquid name>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to imbibe a liquid.  If you have a liquid
    container in your inventory you can drink from that by typing
    the name of the container as the argument.  You can also do this
    in special places, such as the Meeting Square of Karsinya that
    have fountains to drink out of.  You can also specify the
    contents of the liquid you wish to drink.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a cup of water in your inventory you wish to drink.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drink cup
    Havok>  You drink the water.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a cup of water in your inventory you wish to drink.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drink water
    Havok>  You drink the water.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You are standing in a room with a fountain and want a drink.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drink fountain
    Havok>  You drink from the fountain.

#
"OBJ DROP"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  drop <obj | all | all.obj | number> [<coins>]
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to move an object from your inventory to
    the ground of the room you are in.  You can drop everything
    at once from your inventory using the "all" argument.  Or you
    can selectively drop all of one particular type of item by
    using the "all." argument, such as "all.dagger".  You can
    drop coins on the ground by specifying a number and the word
    "coins".

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: Your inventory has a spare dagger.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drop dagger
    Havok>  You drop a dagger.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: Your inventory has a bunch of useless gear in it, you need
    to lose some weight so you can pick up a barrel.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drop all
    Havok>  You drop everything you own.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: Your inventory has four spare daggers.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drop all.dagger
    Havok>  You drop a dagger.
            You drop a dagger.
            You drop a dagger.
            You drop a dagger.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You are feeling generous, so you think you'll leave a small
    fortune lying about on the ground.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> drop 1000 coins
    Havok>  You drop 1000 coins.

#
"OBJ EAT"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  eat <food obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command will cause you to eat the target object, provided
    it is food.  Use this when you are hungry and you have food
    in your inventory.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You are hungry and you have a bread in your inventory.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> eat bread
    Havok>  You eat a bread.

#

    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting, sleeping,

    This command is used to see what equipment you are currently wearing
    and what condition it is in.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to see what you are currently wearing and what
    condition it is in.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> equipment
    Havok>  You are using:
            <used as light>      :Nothing.
            <worn on finger>     :Nothing.
            <worn on finger>     :Nothing.
            <worn on neck>       :Nothing.
            <worn on neck>       :Nothing.
            <worn on body>       :a T-shirt..It is in good condition
            <worn on head>       :a Cubs hat..It is in excellent condition
            <worn on legs>       :khaki pants..They are in excellent condition
            <worn on feet>       :sandals..They are in good condition
            <worn on hands>      :Nothing.
            <worn on arms>       :Nothing.
            <worn as shield>     :Nothing.
            <worn about body>    :Nothing.
            <worn about waist>   :Nothing.
            <worn about wrist>   :Nothing.
            <worn about wrist>   :Nothing.
            <wielded>            :Nothing.
            <held>               :Nothing.
            <worn on back>       :Nothing.
            <worn in right ear>  :Nothing.
            <worn in left ear>   :Nothing.
            <worn on eyes>       :Nothing.
            <notched>            :Nothing.

"OBJ EXAMINE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  examine <obj | mob>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command is similar to the 'look' command.  In some
    circumstances it tends to act like an advanced version,
    providing combined information.  For instance if you
    "look bag" you will see just the outer condition of
    the bag, but if you "examine bag" you will see the outer
    condition and the contents of the bag.  To get that
    information using look you would have to "look bag"
    and "look in bag".

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to take a look at a bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> examine bag
    Havok>  You see nothing special..
            When you look inside, you see:
            burlap 87% full (carried) :
            [ 1] a bread
            [ 2] a hat
            [ 3] a complimentary cup
            ...

#
"OBJ FILL"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  fill <liquid container> <liquid container>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command is usually used at a fountain where you can
    fill a liquid container to the brim with whatever liquid
    is in the fountain.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to fill a barrel with water from a fountain.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> fill barrel fountain
    Havok>  a barrel is filled.

#
"OBJ GET"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  get <obj | all | all.obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to pick up something from the ground
    of the room you are in and place it in your inventory.  You
    can pick up a single object, all the objects on the floor,
    or a group of objects.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to pick up a dagger from the ground.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> get dagger
    Havok>  You get a dagger.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You see several daggers and some bread on the ground you wish
    to pick up.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> get all
    Havok>  You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.
            You get a bread.
            OK.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You see several daggers and some bread on the ground, but
    you only wish to pick up the daggers.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> get all.dagger
    Havok>  You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.

#
"OBJ GIVE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  give <obj | all.obj | number> <mob | coins> [<mob>]
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to pass objects and coins from one
    mob to another.  You can give single objects specifying only
    one target,  you can give a group of objects using an "all."
    argument, and if you specify a number, then the keyword "coins"
    and then the name of the mob, you can give gold coins to the
    target.  You can only give objects from your inventory and it
    will appear in the target mob's inventory.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to give Joe a dagger from your inventory.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> give dagger Joe
    Havok>  You give a dagger to Joe.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to give Joe all your daggers from your inventory.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> give all.dagger Joe
    Havok>  You give a dagger to Joe.
            You give a dagger to Joe.
            You give a dagger to Joe.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to give Joe some gold.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> give 1000 coins Joe
    Havok>  You give 1000 coins to Joe.

#
"OBJ GRAB"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  grab <obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This allows you to hold an object in a free hand (one that is
    not wielding a weapon, or already holding an item).  You must
    hold some objects to use them, such as wands and staffs.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to hold on to a staff.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> grab staff
    Havok>  You grab a staff and hold it.

#
"OBJ HOLD"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  hold <obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This allows you to hold an object in a free hand (one that is
    not wielding a weapon, or already holding an item).  You must
    hold some objects to use them, such as wands and staffs.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to hold on to a staff.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> hold staff
    Havok>  You grab a staff and hold it.

#
"OBJ INVENTORY"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  inventory
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting, sleeping,
                   stunned

    This command will show you what you currently carry in your inventory.
    Your inventory is where you do most of your object organization.  When
    you 'get' an object up off the ground, it appears in your inventory.
    When you 'remove' an object that you are wearing, it appears in your
    inventory.  It is a temporary storage place for equipment.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to see what you have in your inventory.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> inventory
    Havok>  [ 1] a bread
            [ 2] a cup
            [ 3] a dagger[4]
            [ 7] a hat
            ...

#
"OBJ JUNK"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  junk <obj | all.obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command can be considered a cleanup command for equipment.  Whatever
    equipment in your inventory you target with this command will be deleted
    from the game.  Gone, period.  Use this for things that are useless to
    you and anybody else you know.  It also accepts the "all." argument to
    clear out a selection of items, which can be useful in clearing out large
    amounts of useless things, such as scraps from ruined equipment.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to junk a dagger that you have in your inventory.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> junk dagger
    Havok>  You junk a dagger.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have several daggers and some bread in your inventory, but
    you only wish to junk the daggers.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> junk all.dagger
    Havok>  You junk a dagger.
            You junk a dagger.
            You junk a dagger.

#
"OBJ LOCK"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  lock <lockable obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command can be used to lock a container object, provided
    it is lockable, and you have the correct key.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to lock a chest, and you have the correct key.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> lock chest
    Havok>  *Cluck*

#
"OBJ LOOK"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  look [<in | at>] <obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command has many uses, this help deals with looking at
    objects.  For help on other uses of 'look' see "help info look".
    If an object is a container object, using the keyword "in" allows
    you to see the contents of that object.  The keyword "at" is not
    necessary, but can be used to look at the exterior of an object.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to take a look at a bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> look bag
    Havok>  You see nothing special..

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to take a look at a bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> look at bag
    Havok>  You see nothing special..

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to take a look at what is in a bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> look in bag
    Havok>  burlap 87% full (carried) :
            [ 1] a bread
            [ 2] a hat
            [ 3] a complimentary cup
            ...

#
"OBJ OPEN"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  open <container obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command is used to open a container object, provided
    it is unlocked.  Once opened, you can 'get' or 'put' items
    into the container.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to open a chest, which is unlocked.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> open chest
    Havok>  Ok.

#
"OBJ POUR"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  pour <liquid container obj> <liquid container obj | out>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing

    This command is used to empty or transfer liquids from liquid containers.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a barrel of beer that you wish to empty, so that you
    can fill it with water.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> pour barrel out
    Havok>  You empty the barrel.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a barrel of beer that you wish to transfer to a mug.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> pour barrel mug
    Havok>  You pour the beer into the mug.

#
"OBJ PUT"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  put <obj | all | all.obj> <container obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to place an object inside of a container
    object, such as a bag.  The keyword "all" can be used to try
    to put everything in your inventory into the container object.
    Or the keyword "all." to place all of one type of object into
    the container object.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to place a dagger into your bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> put dagger bag
    Havok>  You put a dagger in a bag

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have several daggers and some bread in your inventory
    that you wish to place in a bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> put all bag
    Havok>  a dagger : OK
            a dagger : OK
            a dagger : OK
            a bread : OK.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have several daggers and some bread in your inventory
    and you wish to place the daggers in a bag.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> put all.dagger bag
    Havok>  You put a dagger in a bag
            You put a dagger in a bag
            You put a dagger in a bag

#
"OBJ QUAFF"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  quaff <potion obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to drink potions and gain whatever special
    effects they might bestow.  Care should be given before quaffing
    unknown potions.  While it is possible to quaff potions while
    fighting, it is more likely that the potion bottle breaks before you
    can drink from it.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to drink a potion of healing.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> quaff potion-healing
    Havok>  You quaff a potion of healing which dissolves.
            You feel better!

#
"OBJ QUEST TOKEN"

    If you should happen to find a quest token during your travels,
    it will be replaced by a quest potion, which can be quaffed
    to permanently bestow a 'quest point' on that character.

#
"OBJ REMOVE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  remove <equipped obj | number list | all>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to remove an equipped item and place it in
    your inventory.  You can either specify the object to be removed,
    the placement on the equipped list it occupies, or "all" of your
    equipment.  Most commonly you would specify the object to be removed.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to remove the sandals you are wearing.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> remove sandals
    Havok>  You stop using sandals.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to remove the first 2 things you are wearing and
    the seventh thing you are wearing.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> remove 1,2,7
    Havok>  You stop using the T-shirt.
            You stop using the Cubs cap.
            You stop using a watch.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to remove all you are wearing and go naked.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> remove all
    Havok>  You stop using a T-shirt
            You stop using a Cubs hat
            You stop using khaki pants
            You stop using sandals

#
"OBJ SIP"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  sip <liquid container>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command can be used to take a small drink from a drink
    container.  It will have a smaller effect than a full 'drink',
    but it will still poison you for a short while if the liquid
    is poisoned.  It will also tell you what kind of liquid is
    in the container.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to verify that the barrel you have is filled with
    water.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> sip barrel
    Havok>  It tastes like water.

#
"OBJ TAKE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  take <obj | all | all.obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to pick up something from the ground
    of the room you are in and place it in your inventory.  You
    can pick up a single object, all the objects on the floor,
    or a group of objects.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to pick up a dagger from the ground.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> take dagger
    Havok>  You get a dagger.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You see several daggers and some bread on the ground you wish
    to pick up.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> take all
    Havok>  You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.
            You get a bread.
            OK.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You see several daggers and some bread on the ground, but
    you only wish to pick up the daggers.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> take all.dagger
    Havok>  You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.
            You get a dagger.

#
"OBJ TASTE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  taste <food obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command will cause you to 'eat' a small portion of a food
    object.  If the food is big enough, there will still be some
    remaining.  It will still cause you to be poisoned for a short
    period of time, but less than if you ate the whole thing.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to take a taste of some bread, to see if it is
    poisoned or not.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> taste bread
    Havok>  You taste the bread

#
"OBJ UNLOCK"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  unlock <container obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command is used to unlock a container object, provided
    you have the appropriate key.  After it is unlocked you can
    'open' it and 'look' at it's contents.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You want to unlock a chest that you have the proper key to.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> unlock chest
    Havok>  *Click*

#
"OBJ USE"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  use <obj> [<obj | mob>]
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting

    This command gives you the ability to activate some objects that
    have special effects, such as staves and wands.  If you are holding
    a staff or wand object, you can 'use' it to generate it's effect.
    Each staff or wand will have a different usage, so the targeting
    of the effect is determined by the spell cast by the object.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You are holding a wand of magic missile and wish to target
    an orc with it.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> use wand orc
    Havok>  You point a wand of magic missile at an orc.

#
"OBJ WEAR"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  wear <obj | all> [<wear position>]
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to wear a piece of equipment, moving it
    from your inventory to your equipment list.  If a piece of
    equipment can be worn on multiple locations, such as a cape
    which might be worn on the neck, or about the body, you can
    specify the position you wish to wear it on.  Something
    like a ring, which can only be worn on the finger, does not
    need any extra arguments.  The "all" keyword can be used
    to attempt to wear everything current in your inventory.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a Cubs hat that you wish to wear.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> wear hat
    Havok>  a Cubs hat :You wear a Cubs hat on your head.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a bandanna that you can wear on your head or on
    your neck.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> wear bandanna neck
    Havok>  a bandanna :You wear a bandanna on your neck.

#
"OBJ WIELD"
    Usable by   :  All 1
    Usage       :  wield <weapon obj>
    Positions   :  mounted, standing, fighting, sitting, resting

    This command is used to wield a weapon object, just as you
    use the 'wear' command to wear armor objects.

    (Situation, what you type at the prompt, the message you should see):
    Situation: You have a dagger in your inventory that you wish to use
    in combat, so you must wield it.
    H:50/50 M:120/120 V:100/100> wield dagger
    Havok>  You wield a dagger.

#
"RACE AVARIEL"

    This race of winged elves is the only race currently able
    to fly without magical aid of any kind.  Their wings are
    fragile, especially vulnerable to fire, and can get tired
    if used for extended periods of time.  Very nimble, they
    receive a +2 bonus to dexterity, but they are also
    relatively fragile, and have a -2 penalty to
    their constitution.  See 'help race class combinations'
    for their classes and level limits.

    Infravision
    Flying
    Resist Charm Spells
    Average Height: 4'7"
    Average Weight: 80 pounds
    Size Classification: Small
    Life Span: 1000 years
